## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations (dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration of an oscillator and the available state variable is position x (with optional explicit time dependence t), which matches conservative/nonconservative oscillator models where acceleration is a restoring-force function of x and possibly a time-periodic forcing or parametric modulation in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (Hooke restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small-amplitude oscillations about stable equilibrium)
- Linear oscillator with bias/equilibrium shift: dv_dt = -c0 * (x - c1) (oscillation around displaced equilibrium)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 (stronger amplitude-dependent frequency shift)
- Nonlinear stiffness via absolute value (piecewise-smooth spring): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x * Abs(x) (different effective stiffness for large |x|)
- Double-well (bistable) restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (two stable equilibria, barrier at x=0)
- Pendulum-type restoring (full nonlinearity): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) (angular oscillator beyond small-angle approximation)
- Saturating restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * tanh(c1 * x) (bounded acceleration/restoring at large displacement)
- Periodic external drive (additive forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t) (forced oscillator with drive frequency c2)
- Multi-harmonic drive: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t) + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (general periodic forcing)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (Mathieu-type parametrically driven oscillator)
- Polynomial stiffness with parametric modulation: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * x**3 (parametric Duffing)
- Non-autonomous equilibrium shift: dv_dt = -c0 * (x - c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (moving potential minimum / base excitation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd restoring-force symmetry: dv_dt being an odd function of x (e.g., -c*x, -c*x - d*x**3, -c*sin(k*x)) indicates a symmetric potential about x=0.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness: the sign and magnitude of the x**3 term in dv_dt = -c0*x - c1*x**3 control whether frequency increases (hardening) or decreases (softening) with amplitude.
- Bistability signature: dv_dt = c0*x - c1*x**3 implies a double-well potential with two stable equilibria at nonzero x and an unstable one near x=0.
- Pendulum nonlinearity: sin(c*x) structure implies amplitude-dependent period and non-polynomial restoring behavior (large-angle effects).
- Bounded restoring/acceleration: tanh(c*x) or similar saturating nonlinearities suggest physical limits (e.g., actuator saturation or geometric constraints).
- Parametric resonance indicators: multiplicative time-periodic modulation (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t)) * x suggests Mathieu-type instability bands depending on c2 relative to the natural frequency.
- External forcing indicators: additive periodic terms in t (cos/sin) indicate driven response, possible resonance peaks at the forcing frequency.
- Non-smooth stiffness/impacts: presence of Abs(x) (e.g., x*Abs(x)) suggests piecewise stiffness, contact, or different regimes for positive/negative displacement magnitude.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO1)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - omega0**c0*x - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidate formulas: 51

GT (fixed):
\[
0.422619160916855\sin(t)\;-\;1.15357191344644\,x\;-\;1.15357191344644\,x\,e^{-|x|}
\]
So any matching candidate must be exactly of the form
- one pure sinusoid in \(t\) with no \(x\)-dependence: \(A\sin(t)\) (or \(A\cos(t+\phi)\), etc.),
- plus a linear term in \(x\): \(Bx\),
- plus \(Cx e^{-|x|}\) (note the exponent is \(-|x|\), not \(+|x|\)),
- and **no other** \(t\)-terms, \(x\)-nonlinearities, logs, extra constants, etc., unless their coefficients can be set to 0.

Also: \(\exp(c5\,|x|)\) can match \(\exp(-|x|)\) by setting \(c5=-1\). And \(\sin(c1+c2 t)\) can match \(\sin(t)\) by choosing \(c2=1\) and \(c1=0\) (or other phase-equivalent choices).

---

### 1. \(c0\sin(c1+c2 t)+c3 x+c4 x e^{c5|x|}+c6\cos(c7 t)\)
Set \(c6=0\) to remove extra cosine. Choose \(c2=1,c1=0\). Choose \(c5=-1\). Then match coefficients with \(c0=0.422619160916855\), \(c3=-1.15357191344644\), \(c4=-1.15357191344644\). **Matches.**

### 2. Same but \(+c6 x\cos(c7 t)\)
The \(x\cos(\cdot)\) term is not in GT; must set \(c6=0\). Then it reduces to the same structure as (1) without the extra cosine. With \(c2=1,c1=0,c5=-1\) and coefficients matched, **matches**.

### 3. \(c0\sin(\cdot)+c3 x+c4 x e^{c5|x|}+c6 x+c7 x\cos(\cdot)\)
Need no \(x\cos\) term ⇒ set \(c7=0\). Then linear-in-\(x\) terms combine: \((c3+c6)x\). Choose \(c5=-1\), \(c2=1,c1=0\), \(c0=0.4226...\), \(c4=-1.1535...\), and \(c3+c6=-1.1535...\). **Matches.**

### 4. Has extra \(c6\exp(c7\cos(c8 t))\)
This is a non-sinusoidal \(t\)-dependence; must set \(c6=0\). Then reduces to base form like (1). With same choices, **matches**.

### 5. Includes \(c6\log(c7\sin(c8 x+c9)+1)\)
This introduces non-GT \(x\)-dependence; set \(c6=0\). Remaining terms: \(c0 x + c1\cos(c2 t+c3)+c4 x e^{c5|x|}\). Cosine can match sine via phase shift. Choose \(c5=-1\), and set cosine to equal \(0.4226\sin t\) by e.g. \(c1=0.422619160916855,\ c2=1,\ c3=-\pi/2\). Set \(c0=-1.15357191344644,\ c4=-1.15357191344644\). **Matches.**

### 6. Has extra \(c6 x\cos(c7 t+c8)\)
Need it gone ⇒ set \(c6=0\). Then same as (5) without log; as argued, **matches**.

### 7. Has extra \(c7 x^3\cos(c8 t)\)
Not in GT; set \(c7=0\). Then it’s base form plus an extra \(c6 x\) that can be absorbed into linear coefficient. Choose \(c5=-1\), \(c2=1,c1=0\), and match. **Matches.**

### 8. Two sinusoidal-in-\(t\) terms: \(c0\sin(\cdot)+c7\sin(\cdot)\) plus linear/xexp
Sum of two sines of same frequency can be represented as a single sine with phase, so it can still match \(0.4226\sin t\) by appropriate parameter choices (e.g. set one amplitude 0, or choose both to combine). Also choose \(c5=-1\), and linear coefficient via \(c3+c6\). **Matches.**

### 9. Has \(c6\log(c7 e^{c8 x}+1)\cos(c9 t)\)
This is a product of \(x\)-function and \(t\)-cosine; GT has no such coupling. Only way is \(c6=0\). Then reduces to base form (1) and **matches** with standard choices.

### 10. Has extra \(\sin(c7 x+c8)\)
Not in GT; set \(c6=0\). Remaining is like (5) and **matches**.

Two independent \(t\)-sinusoids can be combined into one sinusoid of frequency 1 if both use same frequency; easiest: set one coefficient to 0. Set \(c6=0\) and use cosine-with-phase to match GT sine. With \(c5=-1\) and linear terms matched, **matches**.
